        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsami.0c22464"><meta property="og:title" content="Autonomous Self-Healing Strategy for Stable Sodium-Ion Battery: A Case Study of Black Phosphorus Anodes"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.0c22464/asset/images/acsami.0c22464.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="Autonomic self-healing (SH), namely, the ability to repair damages from mechanical stress spontaneously, is polarizing attention in the field of new-generation electrochemical devices. This property is highly attractive to enhance the durability of rechargeable Li-ion batteries (LIBs) or Na-ion batteries (SIBs), where high-performing anode active materials (silicon, phosphorus, etc.) are strongly affected by volume expansion and phase changes upon ion insertion. Here, we applied a SH strategy, based on the dynamic quadruple hydrogen bonding, to nanosized black phosphorus (BP) anodes for Na-ion cells. The goal is to overcome drastic capacity decay and short lifetime, resulting from mechanical damages induced by the volumetric expansion/contraction upon sodiation/desodiation. Specifically, we developed novel ureidopyrimidinone (UPy)-telechelic systems and related blends with poly(ethylene oxide) as novel and green binders alternative to the more conventional ones, such as polyacrylic acid and carboxymethylcellulose, which are typically used in SIBs. BP anodes show impressively improved (more than 6 times) capacity retention when employing the new SH polymeric blend. In particular, the SH electrode still works at a current density higher than 3.5 A g–1, whereas the standard BP electrode exhibits very poor performances already at current densities lower than 0.5 A g–1. This is the result of better adhesion, buffering properties, and spontaneous damage reparation."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.0c22464/asset/images/acsami.0c22464.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/nwyw~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="90da87218abfb325-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da87218abfb325-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: '160820cb-1827-4881-a113-f44058fa1421'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

        <script async="" type="text/javascript" src="https://www.googletagservices.com/tag/js/gpt.js" rel="preconnect" nonce="90da87218abfb325-SJC"></script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da87218abfb325-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'applied_materials_interfaces';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

href="/action/showCitFormats?doi=10.1021/acsami.0c22464&amp;href=/doi/10.1021/acsami.0c22464" title="Cite This" class="figure-viewer-cite-this-link"><i class="icon-check-circle"></i><span><strong>Cite <script nonce="90da87218abfb325-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "aamick";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Autonomous Self-Healing Strategy for Stable Sodium-Ion Battery: A Case Study of Black Phosphorus Anodes", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.0c22464", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Autonomous Self-Healing Strategy for Stable Sodium-Ion Battery: A Case Study of Black Phosphorus Anodes", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.0c22464", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Autonomous Self-Healing Strategy for Stable Sodium-Ion Battery: A Case Study of Black Phosphorus Anodes", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.0c22464", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Autonomous Self-Healing Strategy for Stable Sodium-Ion Battery: A Case Study of Black Phosphorus Anodes", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.0c22464", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Autonomous Self-Healing Strategy for Stable Sodium-Ion Battery: A Case Study of Black Phosphorus Anodes", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.0c22464", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Autonomous Self-Healing Strategy for Stable Sodium-Ion Battery: A Case Study of Black Phosphorus Anodes", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.0c22464", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Autonomous Self-Healing Strategy for Stable Sodium-Ion Battery: A Case Study of Black Phosphorus Anodes", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.0c22464", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Autonomous Self-Healing Strategy for Stable Sodium-Ion Battery: A Case Study of Black Phosphorus Anodes", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.0c22464", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Autonomous Self-Healing Strategy for Stable Sodium-Ion Battery: A Case Study of Black Phosphorus Anodes", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.0c22464", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

                                <div role="tooltip" id="tooltip-cc-text-header" class="article__hover"><div class="article__tooltip" data-id="article_drawer_CC-Tooltip"><h3>License Summary*</h3><p>You are free to <span class="bold">share </span>(copy and redistribute) this article in any medium or format and to <span class="bold">adapt </span>(remix, transform, and build upon) the material for any purpose, even commercially within the parameters below:</p><ul><li><img src="/specs/products/achs/releasedAssets/images/cc-license/cc.svg" alt="cc licence" width="22" height="22"><p>Creative Commons (CC): This is a Creative Commons license.</p></li><li><img src="/specs/products/achs/releasedAssets/images/cc-license/by.svg" alt="ny licence" width="22" height="22"><p>Attribution (BY): Credit must be given to the creator.</p></li></ul><a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by/4.0/" class="bold" data-id="article_drawer_CC-License_Tooltip_Link">View full license</a><div class="disclaimer"><p class="bold">*Disclaimer</p><p>This summary highlights only some of the key features and terms of the
                                                actual license. It is not a license and has no legal value. Carefully
                                                review the actual license before using these materials.
                                            </p></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="article_header-metrics-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="article_header-metrics-dropzone"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.0c22464/asset/images/medium/am0c22464_0011.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.0c22464/asset/images/large/am0c22464_0011.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.0c22464&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">Autonomic self-healing (SH), namely, the ability to repair damages from mechanical stress spontaneously, is polarizing attention in the field of new-generation electrochemical devices. This property is highly attractive to enhance the durability of rechargeable Li-ion batteries (LIBs) or Na-ion batteries (SIBs), where high-performing anode active materials (silicon, phosphorus, <i>etc.</i>) are strongly affected by volume expansion and phase changes upon ion insertion. Here, we applied a SH strategy, based on the dynamic quadruple hydrogen bonding, to nanosized black phosphorus (BP) anodes for Na-ion cells. The goal is to overcome drastic capacity decay and short lifetime, resulting from mechanical damages induced by the volumetric expansion/contraction upon sodiation/desodiation. Specifically, we developed novel ureidopyrimidinone (UPy)-telechelic systems and related blends with poly(ethylene oxide) as novel and green binders alternative to the more conventional ones, such as polyacrylic acid and carboxymethylcellulose, which are typically used in SIBs. BP anodes show impressively improved (more than 6 times) capacity retention when employing the new SH polymeric blend. In particular, the SH electrode still works at a current density higher than 3.5 A g<sup>–1</sup>, whereas the standard BP electrode exhibits very poor performances already at current densities lower than 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup>. This is the result of better adhesion, buffering properties, and spontaneous damage reparation.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under</p><div class="article__cc-license__inter"><div class="article__cc-license--hoverable"><a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by/4.0/" aria-describedby="tooltip-cc-text" class="link--bold" data-id="article_abstract_CC-License">CC-BY 4.0
                                    <span class="arrow"></span></a>
                                .

class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Self-healing+Binder&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_self-healing%20binder">self-healing binder</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Supramolecular+Polymers&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_supramolecular%20polymers">supramolecular polymers</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Quadruple+Hydrogen+Bonding&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_quadruple%20hydrogen%20bonding">quadruple hydrogen bonding</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Black+Phosphorus&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_black%20phosphorus">black phosphorus</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Na-ion+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_Na-ion%20batteries">Na-ion batteries</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">1.  Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The future next-generation metal (M)-ion batteries [M = Li-ion batteries (LIBs) and Na-ion batteries (SIBs)] need to be improved in terms of enhanced durability, lower cost per stored energy, and sustainability. Some of the most crucial issues which are detrimental on the battery performances are related to the physical chemistry of the electroactive materials selected as anode components. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1" aria-label="reference 1">(1)</a> The electrochemical processes taking place in the anode compartment, in fact, involve dimensional/structural evolutions which cause degeneration, damage, and serious cycling failure. This is particular evident in anodes based on silicon <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref2" aria-label="reference 2">(2)</a> or phosphorus, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3" aria-label="reference 3">(3)</a> which normally undergo huge volumetric expansion/contraction upon full Li or Na insertion/deinsertion, thereby forcing large material strains. This results in electrode mechanical fracture, leading to cracking, pulverization, loss of electrical contact with the current collector, and even uncontrolled solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) growth. All the previously reported Si- and P-based anodes showed capacity fading higher than 70–80% over the first 10–20 cycles. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2 ref3'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref2 ref3" aria-label="reference 2 and 3">(2,3)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">Several approaches were discussed in the literature to enhance the durability of Si and P anodes in order to exploit their high theoretical capacity, such as the use of nanostructures or composites with carbon acting as a buffer agent. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5 ref6'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5 ref6" aria-label="reference 2 to 6">(2−6)</a> Very recently, an innovative strategy to overcome such concerns is emerging, which finds inspiration from biology and specifically from the capability of some materials/tissues to self-heal or recover from a physical damage to prevent them from the loss of their vital functions. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7" aria-label="reference 7">(7)</a> In this frame, polymers are particularly appealing because of their good self-healing (SH) capabilities involving either physical (<i>e.g.</i>, interchain diffusion, phase-separated morphology, and shape memory effects) or chemical (incorporation of covalent, free radical, or supramolecular dynamic bonds) features, which employ a synergistic combination of hydrogen bonds (HBs), van der Waals forces, and chemical reactions to repair microdamages, autonomously or even upon external triggering by variation of pH, temperature, pressure, and so forth. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7 ref8 ref9 ref10 ref11'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7 ref8 ref9 ref10 ref11" aria-label="reference 7 to 11">(7−11)</a> SH polymers (SHPs) are finding applications as active components in the improvement of electrochemical energy storage devices, including LIBs. For this specific application, several possible recovering strategies were explored, including different healing mechanisms (physical <i>vs</i> chemical), processes, and materials. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12 ref13 ref14'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12 ref13 ref14" aria-label="reference 12 to 14">(12−14)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">In order to develop new electrodes with high energy density and less irreversible mechanical fractures, SPHs were added chiefly to microparticles of silicon, both pure and as composites with carbon. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15 ref16 ref17 ref18 ref19'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15 ref16 ref17 ref18 ref19" aria-label="reference 15 to 19">(15−19)</a> In this frame, SHPs acted as a new concept of binder, properly designed to be multifunctional as (i) a mechanical stabilizer, (ii) a structural support, (iii) wettable by the electrolyte, and also (iv) capable of recovering the physical damage caused by the structural changes. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20" aria-label="reference 20">(20)</a> Basically, SPHs were used following two different approaches: (i) as a thin soft layer of randomly branched hydrogen-bonded strands coating the Si electrode <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18" aria-label="reference 18">(18)</a> or (ii) as a conventional binder surrounding the electrode particles and binding them to the current collector. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a> In both cases, very promising results were obtained in terms of cracks and damages recover upon cycling and, consequently, significant improvements in terms of anode capacity retention. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14 ref19 ref22'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14 ref19 ref22" aria-label="reference 14, 19 and 22">(14,19,22)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">Among the possible SH mechanisms, such as covalent bonding, supramolecular chemistry, ion–ion interaction, π–π-stacking, and dynamic H-bonding, the latter one received specific attention in the case of battery application. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14 ref22 ref23 ref24'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14 ref22 ref23 ref24" aria-label="reference 14 and 22 to 24">(14,22−24)</a> In fact, even though H-bonds among neutral systems are not particularly strong, they confer significant mechanical strength due to the high directionality and affinity. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7" aria-label="reference 7">(7)</a> This is well evident, especially if multiple H-bonds are combined into a functional unit, for example, ureidopyrimidinone (UPy), which strongly associates with polymers potentially adaptable to the battery components (<i>e.g.</i>, polyethers). In this case, the mechanism is dynamic and requires high free volume and fluid-like systems which allow the orientation and approaching of the polymer chains, thus favoring the H–H interactions and consequently the SH mechanism. These supramolecular polymers exhibit low glass transition temperature, <i>T</i><sub>g</sub>, resulting in soft systems with high segmental motion, easily modeled, but mechanically strong. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8 ref11'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref8 ref11" aria-label="reference 8 and 11">(8,11)</a> Furthermore, an SHP based on dynamic bonding is capable of repeated and spontaneous healing without any external stimulus <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11 ref25'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref11 ref25" aria-label="reference 11 and 25">(11,25)</a> even at room temperature, as in the case of UPy-containing brush-like poly(ethylene glycol) (PEG) chains <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24" aria-label="reference 24">(24)</a> or upon gentle heating, as shown by maleimide–furan-based polymers. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26" aria-label="reference 26">(26)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">If silicon anodes have been widely investigated in terms of SH strategies, very few examples are to date reported about phosphorus but for a work employing inorganic anchoring units to protect the active material surface. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27" aria-label="reference 27">(27)</a></div><div class="NLM_p last">In this paper, we describe, for the first time to the best of our knowledge, an autonomic SH strategy to improve the cycling lifetime of black phosphorus (BP) anodes for SIBs. To this aim, a novel H-bonding directed polymer is developed as an electrode binder with the specific role to repair the mechanical damages induced by the BP huge expansion and strain upon cycling. The system is based on PEG telechelic polymers decorated with UPy-chain end functionalities exhibiting the ability to self-recover at room temperature in the absence of external stimuli. The SH capability of the polymer is investigated by means of a multitechnique approach. Its effect on the BP anode electrochemical performances is demonstrated by comparing with similar electrodes including conventional binders, such as polyacrylic acid (PAA) and carboxymethylcellulose (CMC).</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">2.  Materials and Methods</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec2_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4">2.1.  Materials</h3><div class="NLM_p last">Compound UPy-NCO 1 was synthesized as reported elsewhere. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28" aria-label="reference 28">(28)</a> Di-(OH)-terminated PEGs were purchased with different molecular weights (PEG<sub><i>n</i></sub>, <i>M</i><sub>W</sub> = 4000 Da, <i>n</i> = 91; <i>M</i><sub>W</sub> = 6000 Da, <i>n</i> = 136; <i>M</i><sub>W</sub> = 10,000 Da, <i>n</i> = 227; and <i>M</i><sub>W</sub> = 35,000 Da, <i>n</i> = 795) as monodisperse products from different commercial sources and were used as received. All other commercially available compounds were used as received.</div></div><div id="sec2_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i5">2.2.  Synthesis of UPyPEG<sub><i>n</i></sub>UPy (2–5) Polymers: PEG 2-(6-Isocyanato-hexilaminocarbonylamino)-6-metyl-4-[1<i>H</i>]-pyrimidinone</h3><div class="NLM_p">The representative procedure for the synthesis of all the polymers 2–5, sketched in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#sch1" aria-label="Scheme 1">Scheme </a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#sch1" aria-label="1">1</a>, is reported in detail for the specific polymer 5 (UPyPEG<sub>795</sub>UPy).</div><figure id="sch1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Scheme 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.0c22464/asset/images/medium/am0c22464_0010.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.0c22464/asset/images/large/am0c22464_0010.jpeg" id="gr9" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><div class="title2">Scheme 1. Synthesis by UPy-Terminated PEG Telechelics (UPyPEG<sub><i>n</i></sub>UPy) Developed in This Paper<sup>a</sup></div></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.0c22464/asset/images/large/am0c22464_0010.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.0c22464&amp;id=sch1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div><p class="last"></p><p class="last"><span class="fn-label"><sup>a</sup></span>Reaction conditions: dry CHCl<sub>3</sub>, dibutyltin dilaurate (cat.), 60 °C, and 48 h.</p><p></p></figure><div class="NLM_p last">UPy-NCO 1 (166.4 mg, 0.568 mmol) was added to a solution of PEG<sub>795</sub> (5 g, 0.143 mmol) in CHCl<sub>3</sub> previously dried over molecular sieves (10 mL) in the presence of a catalytic amount of dibutyltin dilaurate (two drops). The resulting reaction mixture was stirred at 60 °C under inert atmosphere for 48 h. The mixture was cooled and filtered off to remove the exceeding UPy-NCO (compound 1). The last purification step was precipitation in hexane. The precipitate was recovered by filtration and washed plentifully with hexane, followed by drying under a reduced pressure to obtain UPyPEG<sub><i>n</i></sub>UPy as a white powder (4,9 g, 97%). <sup>1</sup>H NMR of UPyPEG<sub>795</sub>UPy (200 MHz, CDCl<sub>3</sub>): δ 5.89 (s, 2H, CH═CCH<sub>3</sub>), 4.07 (d, <i>J</i> = 6.9 Hz, 4H, OCH<sub>2</sub>(CH<sub>2</sub>OCH<sub>2</sub>)CH<sub>2</sub>O), 4.02–3.17 (m, 2093H, OCH<sub>2</sub>(CH<sub>2</sub>OCH<sub>2</sub>)CH<sub>2</sub>O), 3.11 (m, 8H, NH(C═O)NHCH<sub>2</sub> + CH<sub>2</sub>NH(C═O)O), 2.15 (s, 6H, CH<sub>3</sub>C═CH), 1.48 (m, 8H, NHCH<sub>2</sub>CH<sub>2</sub> + CH<sub>2</sub>CH<sub>2</sub>NHC═O), 1.34 (m, 8H, CH<sub>2</sub>CH<sub>2</sub>CH<sub>2</sub>CH<sub>2</sub>CH<sub>2</sub>CH<sub>2</sub>). <sup>13</sup>C NMR (75 MHz, CDCl<sub>3</sub>): δ = 172.8, 156.3, 154.4, 148.1, 106.4, 42.6, 39.5, 30.9, 29.1, 26.0, 19.9, 15.7.</div></div><div id="sec2_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i7" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i7">2.3.  Preparation of SH Blends of (UPyPEG<sub>795</sub>UPy)—PEO</h3><div class="NLM_p">Three blends of UPyPEG<sub>795</sub>UPy and PEO (300 kDa) were obtained by mixing UPyPEG<sub>795</sub>UPy and PEO in deionized water at different volume concentrations 40/60 (40–60), 50/50 (50–50), and 60/40 (60–40) (see <a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">Table </a><a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">1</a>). The final mixture was then cast on a Teflon foil and dried at 50 °C under vacuum in order to obtain homogeneous 110 μm-thick films.</div><div class="NLM_table-wrap" id="tbl1"><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption"><div class="NLM_caption" id=""><div class="title2">Table 1. Glass Transition Temperatures, <i>T</i><sub>g</sub>, Melting Enthalpies, Δ<i>H</i><sub>m,s</sub>, and Crystalline Fraction, <i>X</i><sub><i>c</i></sub>, (Estimated from <sup>1</sup>H and
