            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Research</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Abstr.: Self-healing is the capability of a material to recover from phys. damage.  Both phys. and chem. approaches have been used to construct self-healing polymers.  These include diffusion and flow, shape-memory effects, heterogeneous self-healing systems, covalent-bond reformation and reshuffling, dynamics of supramol. chem. or combinations thereof.  In this Review, we discuss the similarities and differences between approaches to achieve self-healing in synthetic polymers, where possible placing this discussion in the context of biol. systems.  In particular, we highlight the role of thermal transitions, network heterogeneities, localized chem. reactions enabling the reconstruction of damage and phys. reshuffling.  We also discuss energetic and length-scale considerations, as well as scientific and technol. challenges and opportunities.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrhJMm9D6GaEbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg7fVZe3DxmlQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhtlSktLrI&amp;md5=c285a80834858f0f808e83a26c73affa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1039/c3cs60109a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Urban, M.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-healing polymeric materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Ying; Urban, Marek W.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Inspired by nature, self-healing materials represent the forefront of recent developments in materials chem. and engineering.  This review outlines the recent advances in the field of self-healing polymers.  The first part discusses thermodn. requirements for self-healing networks in the context of conformation changes that contribute to the Gibbs free energy.  The chain flexibility significantly contributes to the entropy changes, whereas the heat of reaction and the external energy input are the main contributors to enthalpy changes.  The second part focuses on chem. reactions that lead to self-healing, and the primary classes are the covalent bonding, supramol. assemblies, ionic interactions, chemo-mech. self-healing, and shape memory polymers.  The third part outlines recent advances using encapsulation, remote self-healing and the role of shape memory polymers.  Recent developments in the field of self-healing polymers undeniably indicate that the main challenge will be the designing of high glass transition (Tg) functional materials, which also exhibit stimuli-responsive attributes.  Build-in controllable hierarchical heterogeneousness at various length scales capable of remote self-healing by phys. and chem. responses will be essential in designing future materials of the 21st century.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrrt2wC-OSawLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg7fVZe3DxmlQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXht1Wisb%252FO&amp;md5=3a1082d1d58eadf7b424bd1d32c8e203</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201813525"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chakma, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Konkolewicz, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Dynamic Covalent Bonds in Polymeric Materials</span>. <i>Angew.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Dynamic covalent bonds (DCBs) have received significant attention over the past decade.  These are covalent bonds that are capable of exchanging or switching between several mols.  Particular focus has recently been on utilizing these DCBs in polymeric materials.  Introduction of DCBs into a polymer material provides it with powerful properties including self-healing, shape-memory properties, increased toughness, and ability to relax stresses as well as to change from one macromol. architecture to another.  This Minireview summarizes commonly used powerful DCBs formed by simple, often "click" reactions, and highlights the powerful materials that can result.  Challenges and potential future developments are also discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpAKBmOdhK-zbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg7fVZe3DxmlQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXot1Wjtrk%253D&amp;md5=d2fb71079ad7505d92fc77569c257fd4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201903762"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Development and application of self-healing materials in smart batteries and supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cheng, Yan; Xiao, Xiao; Pan, Kunming; Pang, Huan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The development of rechargeable energy storage devices has received much attention recently, esp. for smart energy storage devices.  This paper reviews the applications and latest developments in recent years of a class of intelligent energy storage devices.  These energy storage devices are made from self-healing materials, and therefore, they have their own self-healing function.  They can not only undergo repeated folding deformations during use but also automatically repair their damaged parts to extend their service life.  We focus on the repair mechanisms and performances of energy storage devices prepd. from self-healing materials with a focus on electrodes and electrolytes.  Since the research on these self-healing materials is still in its infancy, it has developed rapidly but still suffers from many limitations.  Therefore, we discuss the challenges this research is currently facing and the opportunities for future development.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGorWpZL7yzNQLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh1sOX7z6aMMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhs1Ohsb%252FF&amp;md5=191fc7d5892950ae24e8eaf57b0cf144</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1002/celc.201801612"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Advances on Self-Healing Materials and Batteries</span>. <i>ChemElectroChem</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>6</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1605</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1622</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent Advances on Self-Healing Materials and Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Hua; Wang, Panpan; Feng, Yuping; Liu, Jie; Wang, Jiaqi; Hu, Mengmeng; Wei, Jun; Huang, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemElectroChem</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Self-healing is a concept to imitate the healing of biol. damage and is considered to be an important property of next-generation smart materials.  With a huge breakthrough of self-healing materials in recent years, many devices with integrated self-healing ability are promising due to their intelligence and durability.  Among them, self-healing batteries have attracted ever-growing interest due to their remarkable electrochem. performance and broad application prospects.  In this article, the state-of-the-art progress in self-healing materials and batteries are summarized.  First, this review introduces the main self-healing mechanisms and corresponding materials.  Second, various self-healing batteries including micro and macro self-healing, are discussed, about their self-healing principles, fabrication techniques, and self-healing performances.  Finally, existing challenges and future opportunities are discussed in this thriving field.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqWm9zS8kkz3LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh1sOX7z6aMMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhsVyhu7k%253D&amp;md5=0791e54777f2f75a16396e1078e66b17</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202002815"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mezzomo, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ferrara, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Brugnetti, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Callegari, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Quartarone, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mustarelli, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ruffo, R.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Exploiting Self-Healing in Lithium Batteries: Strategies for Next-Generation Energy Storage Devices</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Exploiting Self-Healing in Lithium Batteries: Strategies for Next-Generation Energy Storage Devices</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mezzomo, Lorenzo; Ferrara, Chiara; Brugnetti, Gabriele; Callegari, Daniele; Quartarone, Eliana; Mustarelli, Piercarlo; Ruffo, Riccardo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Major improvements in stability and performance of batteries are still required for a more effective diffusion in industrial key sectors such as automotive and foldable electronics.  An encouraging route resides in the implementation into energy storage devices of self-healing features, which can effectively oppose the deterioration upon cycling that is typical of these devices.  In order to provide a comprehensive view of the topic, this Review first summarizes the main self-healing processes that have emerged in the multifaceted field of smart materials, classifying them on the basis of their recovering mechanisms.  Then, attention is closely focused on self-healable energy storage devices.  In particular, self-healing in lithium-ion and lithium-metal batteries is discussed, emphasizing both the phys. (cracks, fractures, cuts, etc.) and chem. (degrdn., gas prodn., etc.) issues that currently threaten the operating life of these devices, and the more effective self-healing strategies which can prevent or postpone undesired and dangerous failures.  Finally, an outlook on the possible resoln. of relevant challenges is briefly discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGodITxp0swANLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh1sOX7z6aMMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXitFOgu7jO&amp;md5=321f21ffaa8c8b7943b6df7479e1aa4e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1016/j.joule.2018.02.012"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nuli, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hirano, S.-i.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Silicon Microparticle Anodes with Self-Healing Multiple Network Binder</span>. <i>Joule</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>2</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">950</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">961</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Silicon Microparticle Anodes with Self-Healing Multiple Network Binder</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Zhixin; Yang, Jun; Zhang, Tao; Nuli, Yanna; Wang, Jiulin; Hirano, Shin-ichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Joule</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Cell Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Si has been regarded as a promising anode material for Li-ion batteries.  However, its dramatic vol. change during cycling poses formidable challenges to building stable electrodes.  Since Si microparticles (SiMPs) can easily cause the pulverization and loss of electronic contact, many previous works were focused on porous-structured, nanostructured, or hierarchically structured silicon materials to improve the cycle stability.  However, their low-cost and mass prodn. is mostly difficult or even impossible.  Herein, a water-sol. polymer binder, poly(acrylic acid)-poly(2-hydroxyethyl acrylate-co-dopamine methacrylate), is designed and synthesized.  It shows better wettability to liq. electrolyte than poly(acrylic acid).  Moreover, its multiple network structure with rigid-soft chains and bonds, and special self-healing capability in situ formed during the electrode prepn., not only provides enough mech. support but also buffers the strain caused by the vol. change of SiMPs.  Thus, the cycle stability and rate performance are remarkably improved under high reversible capacity or electrode loading.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp39yR9zrLU4LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh1sOX7z6aMMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtVSmtLjJ&amp;md5=22c7186107419f104f54fc400900ba71</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1016/j.elecom.2017.12.023"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Self-Healing Strategy for Si Nanoparticles towards Practical Application as Anode Materials for Li-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Electrochem.                 <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ECCMF9</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1388-2481</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The overwhelming advantage of Si nanoparticles (SiNPs) over Si microsized particles (SiMPs) as anode materials is compromised by their severe side reactions with electrolyte and agglomeration during cycling.  Unlike usual solns. such as surface encapsulation or coating, here, a new strategy was proposed by mimicking the self-healing ability of living organisms.  Ureidopyrimidinone functionalized polyethylene glycol (UPy-PEG-UPy) was successfully synthesized.  Taking it as binder, SiNPs achieved excellent electrochem. performance with an initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) as high as 81% and a reversible capacity of 1454 mAh/g after 400 cycles corresponding to an av. capacity decay of 0.04% per cycle.  This achievement is attributed to the self-healing ability of UPy-PEG-UPy, which enables to spontaneously heal micro-cracks on electrode prior to its propagation, therefore preventing Si particles agglomeration and maintaining electrode integrity.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrVFplBTajopLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh1sOX7z6aMMA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-healing chemistry enables the stable operation of silicon microparticle anodes for high-energy lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Chao; Wu, Hui; Chen, Zheng; McDowell, Matthew T.; Cui, Yi; Bao, Zhenan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1042-1048</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The ability to repair damage spontaneously, which is termed self-healing, is an important survival feature because it increases the lifetime of most living creatures.  This feature is highly desirable for rechargeable batteries because the lifetime of high-capacity electrodes, such as Si anodes, is shortened by mech. fractures generated during the cycling process.  Here, inspired by nature, the authors apply self-healing chem. to Si microparticle (SiMP) anodes to overcome their short cycle-life.  Anodes made from low-cost SiMPs (∼3-8 μm), for which stable deep galvanostatic cycling was previously impossible, can now have an excellent cycle life when coated with a self-healing polymer.  The authors attain a cycle life 10 times longer than state-of-art anodes made from SiMPs and still retain a high capacity (up to ∼3,000 mA-h g-1).  Cracks and damage in the coating during cycling can be healed spontaneously by the randomly branched H-bonding polymer used.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqYtqL6FJ0YeLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhbzvYvOY1JEA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhslynsrbL&amp;md5=c827d4d624620bd75ca2fe77d56383fc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201908433"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ryu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yoo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, N.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Room-Temperature Crosslinkable Natural Polymer Binder for High-Rate and Stable Silicon Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ryu, Jaegeon; Kim, Sungho; Kim, Jimin; Park, Sooham; Lee, Seungho; Yoo, Seokkeun; Kim, Jangbae; Choi, Nam-Soon; Ryu, Ja-Hyoung; Park, Soojin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Natural polymers with abundant side functionalities are emerging as a promising binder for high-capacity yet large-vol.-change silicon anodes with a strong and reversible supramol. interaction that originates from secondary bonding.  However, the supramol. network solely based on hydrogen bonding is relatively vulnerable to repeated deformation and has an insufficient diffusivity of lithium ions.  Herein, reported is a facile but efficient way of incorporating the natural polymers with an ionically conductive crosslinker, which can construct a robust network for silicon anodes.  The boronic acid in the crosslinker spontaneously reacts with natural polymers to generate boronic esters at room temp. without any kind of triggers, which gives a strong and dynamic covalent bonding to the supramol. network.  The other component in the crosslinker, polyethylene oxide, contributes to the enhanced ionic cond. of polymers, leading to outstanding rate performances even at a high mass loading of silicon nanoparticles (&gt;2 mg cm-2).  The small portion of the proposed crosslinker can modulate the strength of the entire network by balancing the covalent crosslinking and self-healing secondary interaction along with the fast lithium-ion diffusion, thus enabling the extended operation of silicon electrodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrV6Yn2nFHg0bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhbzvYvOY1JEA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXisVyqsLrF&amp;md5=aa0654053c0226107cd306f53faa41ca</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202002508"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Manthiram, A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Review of the Design of Advanced Binders for High-Performance Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Review of the Design of Advanced Binders for High-Performance Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zou, Feng; Manthiram, Arumugam</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Polymer binders as a crit. component in rechargeable batteries provide the electrodes with interconnected structures and mech. strength to maintain the electronic/ionic transfer during battery cycling.  The conventional binders, such as polyvinylidene fluoride (PVDF), are not ideal candidates due to their relatively low adhesiveness, weak mech. strength, and poor functionality for high-energy-d. batteries with a thick electrode and/or a high-capacity electrode.  Nevertheless, the binder has not yet received the attention that reflects its importance in batteries.  The requirements of high energy d. batteries make essential the exploration of advanced polymeric binders, which possess particular functions.  In this review, state-of-the-art binder design strategies are sorted in terms of the challenges of various electrodes (anodes and cathodes for lithium ion batteries (LIBs) and sulfur cathodes for Li-S batteries), which have been commercialized or have the potential for practical cells.  A deep insight into how the polymeric binders improve the cell performance and the design principle of new binders is also provided.  Finally, a perspective on the direction of future binder development for high-energy-d. batteries with long cycle life is presented.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpNdWkavMAIKrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhbzvYvOY1JEA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXitVKrsL%252FE&amp;md5=946f97aa99ff519d9bf96127f199e25a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1002/chem.201900988"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, P.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Polymer Binders Constructed through Dynamic Noncovalent Bonds for High-Capacity Silicon-Based Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Yiyang; Gao, Shilun; Sun, Feiyuan; Yang, Huabin; Cao, Peng-Fei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">47</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10976-10994</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Silicon (Si) is a promising candidate for high-capacity anode materials owing to its high theor. capacity (3579 mAh g-1), low working voltage, and wide natural abundance, although its huge vol. variation during charge/discharge processes always results in a short cycling life.  Polymer binders play a vital role in improving the cycling performance of Si-based anodes, although traditional polyvinylidene difluoride cannot fulfil the requirements owing to its weak van der Waals forces with the Si surface.  Recently, polymer binders constructed by dynamic bonds have been developed, which are reported to allow high-energy-d. electrodes with improved electrochem. performance.  With dynamic bonds including hydrogen bonding, ionic bonding, and host-guest interactions, these polymer binders possess self-healing capabilities and enhanced mech. performance, achieving a tremendous advance in addressing the capacity fading of Si-based anodes.  In this review, we will summarize the research progress of polymer binders constructed with dynamic bonds, and the challenges for their real applications in advanced Li-ion batteries will also be discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrCq3aK6YIgMbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhbzvYvOY1JEA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXht1ynurzF&amp;md5=75d7305f0b035299be2f15999b59ef7a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201703138"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Munaoka, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lopez, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">To, J.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-healing composite polymer electrolyte formed via supramolecular networks for high-performance lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Binghua; Jo, Ye Hyang; Wang, Rui; He, Dan; Zhou, Xingping; Xie, Xiaolin; Xue, Zhigang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10354-10362</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel supramol. network-reinforced and self-healing composite polymer electrolyte (SHCPE) is designed and fabricated via the incorporation of ureido-pyrimidinone (UPy)-functionalized SiO2 (SiO2-UPy) into the polymer matrix contg. UPy units.  The bonded UPy groups on SiO2 could form supramol. networks with the polymer via the interactions of quadruple hydrogen bonding.  Benefitting from the supramol. interactions, the fillers of SiO2-UPy are able to uniformly disperse and reduce the agglomeration.  As a result, the interphase between SiO2 and the polymer matrix, which is crucial to provide a fast conduction channel for lithium ions, is increased.  Consequently, the SHCPE exhibits an enhanced ionic cond. of 8.0 × 10-5 S cm-1 at 30 °C compared with that of the CPE blended with pristine SiO2.  More importantly, the self-healing and mech. properties of the SHCPE are simultaneously improved due to the increase of phys. cross-linked sites in the polymer matrix.  Owing to these outstanding properties, the lithium-ion batteries fabricated using the SHCPE exhibit stable cycling performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq5IWeu32WZ9rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhbzvYvOY1JEA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXlslemt7k%253D&amp;md5=5a8a3e82e23329fac4b8bbfad7426852</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1039/C8TA01907J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xue, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Flexible, Self-Healing and Highly Stretchable Polymer Electrolyte via Quadruple Hydrogen Bonding for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A flexible, self-healing and highly stretchable polymer electrolyte via quadruple hydrogen bonding for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Binghua; He, Dan; Hu, Ji; Ye, Yunsheng; Peng, Haiyan; Zhou, Xingping; Xie, Xiaolin; Xue, Zhigang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Polymer electrolytes are envisioned to be promising alternatives to their liq. counterparts in lithium-ion batteries as they are able to address electrolyte inflammability and leakage issues.  However, polymer electrolytes usually suffer from cracks or breakage, which could lead to short circuits and bring severe safety issues.  Herein, we propose a paradigm to address these problems in which the polymer electrolyte is formed by a phys. cross-linked network via ureidopyrimidinone (UPy) contg. brush-like poly(ethylene glycol) chains.  The formed novel polymer electrolyte is flexible and able to provide fast intrinsic self-healability and high stretchability.  It can heal the cut damage within 2 h under ambient conditions without any external stimulus and can be stretched to more than 20 times its length without breaking.  Furthermore, the novel polymer electrolyte exhibits excellent interfacial stability with electrodes, resulting in high performance batteries with stable reversible electrochem. reaction and cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpMbwlvwRALmbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgC3rkcNHK5AQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXntlelsr0%253D&amp;md5=e786bc79de9a1f6e716bc867b2245cb6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1038/35057232"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">White, S.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Autonomic healing of polymer composites</span></div><div class="casAuthors">White, S. R.; Sottos, N. R.; Geubelle, P. H.; Moore, J. S.; Kessler, M. R.; Sriram, S. R.; Brown, E. N.; Viswanathan, S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature (London, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2001</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">409</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6822</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">794-797</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Structural polymers are susceptible to damage in the form of cracks, which form deep within the structure where detection is difficult and repair is almost impossible.  Cracking leads to mech. degrdn. of fiber-reinforced polymer composites; in microelectronic polymeric components it can also lead to elec. failure.  Microcracking induced by thermal and mech. fatigue is also a long-standing problem in polymer adhesives.  Regardless of the application, once cracks have formed within polymeric materials, the integrity of the structure is significantly compromised.  Expts. exploring the concept of self-repair have been previously reported, but the only successful crack-healing methods that have been reported so far require some form of manual intervention.  Here, a structural polymeric material with the ability to autonomically heal cracks is reported.  The material incorporates a microencapsulated healing agent that is released upon crack intrusion.  Polymn. of the healing agent is then triggered by contact with an embedded catalyst, bonding the crack faces.  The fracture expts. yield as much as 75% recovery in toughness, and the approach may be applicable to other brittle materials systems (including ceramics and glasses).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq2lu4zUvqR0rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgC3rkcNHK5AQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD3MXhsFCjsbg%253D&amp;md5=6c89d4c4b2c83453a81f2a0a99854c4e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1002/macp.201100559"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">van

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The poor elec. cond. and large volumetric changes hinder the practical application of red phosphorus despite its high theor. capacity of 2596 mA h g-1.  A simple approach to overcome this challenge via anchoring sol. lithium-sulfur intermediate compds. on the surface of red phosphorus and configuring an efficient interface is proposed here.  Sulfur is strategically incorporated into phosphorus by P-S bonding to construct a phosphorus-sulfur/carbon composite with a highly conductive interface.  The sol. Li-S intermediates formed during the electrochem. lithiation process could be anchored on the surface of phosphorus by capillary action to heal the cracks/defects of phosphorus caused by volumetric expansion.  Calcns. based on first principles demonstrate that the strategic introduction of sulfur enables band overlapping near the Fermi level, which facilitates high efficiency electron-transfer at the P-S interface and thus improves the overall electrochem. properties of the constructed composite.  Therefore, the phosphorus-sulfur/carbon composite delivers a high initial charge capacity of 1808.2 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1 and maintains a reversible capacity of 935.3 mA h g-1 with a high coulombic efficiency of approx. 99.4% after 200 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoVxOgH7e1zFbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgC3rkcNHK5AQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhvFymsbvO&amp;md5=cfbf006ba9af2c4deaf62388564c111c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201803854"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Mechanically Robust Atomic Oxygen-Resistant Coatings Capable of Autonomously Healing Damage in Low Earth Orbit Space Environment</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Efficiency and Quality Issues in the Production of Black Phosphorus by Mechanochemical Synthesis: A Multi-Technique Approach</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ferrara, Chiara; Vigo, Emanuele; Albini, Benedetta; Galinetto, Pietro; Milanese, Chiara; Tealdi, Cristina; Quartarone, Eliana; Passerini, Stefano; Mustarelli, Piercarlo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Black phosphorus (BP) is a two-dimensional material potentially of great interest for applications in the fields of energy, sensing, and microelectronics.  One of the most interesting methods to obtain BP is the conversion from red phosphorus (RP) by means of high-energy mechanochem. synthesis.  To date, however, this synthesis process was not well characterized.  In this work, starting from the math. model of energy transfer during the ball milling process, we investigate the effects on RP → BP conversion of three exptl. parameters, the rotation speed, the milling time, and the wt. ratio between the spheres and the milled material (BtPw ratio).  The efficiency of the conversion process was verified by solid-state NMR, Raman spectroscopy, and X-ray diffraction.  Whereas the first two parameters have a minor importance, the BtPw ratio plays a primary role in the RP → BP conversion.  Yields approaching 100% can be obtained also with short milling times (15 min) and adequate rotation speed (e.g., 500 r.p.m.), provided that the BtPw ratio &gt;40:1 is used.  These results confirm the energy sustainability of the mechanochem. synthesis approach.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrSgBKOkouJiLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgC3rkcNHK5AQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXkt1Wgu74%253D&amp;md5=4bdff6829e6831fb76114d85e777b0eb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.6b02982"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kwon, Y.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Magnetite (Fe3O4) was used as a model high capacity metal oxide active material to demonstrate advantages derived from consideration of both electron and ion transport in the design of composite battery electrodes.  The conjugated polymer, poly[3-(potassium-4-butanoate) thiophene] (PPBT), was introduced as a binder component, while polyethylene glycol (PEG) was coated onto the surface of Fe3O4 nanoparticles.  The introduction of PEG reduced aggregate size, enabled effective dispersion of the active materials and facilitated ionic conduction.  As a binder for the composite electrode, PPBT underwent electrochem. doping which enabled the formation of effective elec. bridges between the carbon and Fe3O4 components, allowing for more efficient electron transport.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Telechelic oligomers functionalized with 2-ureido-4[1H]-pyrimidone (UPy), a quadruple hydrogen bonding group, have been synthesized using a combination of atom-transfer radical polymn. and click reaction.  Ureidopyrimidone (UPy) synthons with propargyl and azide functionality were used for clicking with azido and propargyl telechelic oligomers, resp.  The effect of triazole linker and types of oligomers differing in Tg and polarity, such as poly(Bu acrylate) (PnBA), polystyrene (PS), and polybutadiene (PBd) on UPy hydrogen bonding have been examd.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hydrogen-bonded supramolecular polymer networks</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lange, Ronald F. M.; Van Gurp, M.; Meijer, E. W.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Polymer Science, Part A: Polymer Chemistry</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The strong dimerizing, quadruple hydrogen-bonding ureido-pyrimidone unit was used to obtain reversible polymer networks via a synthetic route from com. available starting materials.  The hydrogen-bonding ureido-pyrimidone network was prepd. using 3- and 4-isocyanatomethyl-1-methylcyclohexyl-isocyanate (IMCI) in the regioselective coupling reaction of multi-hydroxy functionalized ethylene oxide-propylene oxide copolymers with isocytosines.  1H- and 13C-NMR, IR, MS, and ES-MS anal., performed on a model reaction using butanol, demonstrated the formation of the hydrogen-bonding ureido-pyrimidone unit in a yield of more than 95%.  The well-defined, strong hydrogen-bonding ureido-pyrimidone network was compared with a traditional covalently bonded polymer network, a multi-directional hydrogen-bonded polymer network based on urea units, and a ref. compd.  The advantage of the reversible, hydrogen-bonded polymer networks is the formation of the thermodynamically most favorable products, which show a higher virtual mol. wt. and shear modulus, compared to the irreversible, covalently bonded polymer network.  The properties of the ureido-pyrimidone network are unique; the well-defined and strong dimerization of the ureido-pyrimidone unit does not require any addnl. stabilization such as crystn. or other kinds of phase sepn., and displays a well-defined viscoelastic transition.  The ureido-pyrimidone network represents the first example of a truly reversible polymer network showing these features.  Furthermore, the ureido-pyrimidone dimerization is strong enough to construct supramol. materials possessing acceptable mech. properties.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrDkfgzUZYtbbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj6UmBGgq_2BA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK1MXmt1Gkt74%253D&amp;md5=79d1707b3d2a94132abff851ad514575</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1039/F29726800656"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Afifi-Effat, A.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In this study, inspired by the multiple supramol. interactions in nature including hydrogen bonding and ionic bonds, we proposed a simple strategy to fabricate high-performance dual phys. crosslinked D-hydrogels, which is triggered by the self-complementary quadruple hydrogen bonding interactions between 2-ureido-4[1H]-pyrimidinone (UPy) dimers and Fe3+ ionic coordination bonds as the dynamic sacrificial crosslinkers, thus obviously enhancing the mech. strength and toughness.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Analysis of linear viscoelasticity of a crosslinking polymer at the gel point</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Winter, H.     </div><div class="casAbstract">A very simple memory integral constitutive equation is suggested for the stress in crosslinking polymers at their transition from liq. to solid state (gel point).  The equation allows for only a single material parameter, the strength (Pa s1/2 units), and it is able to describe every known viscoelastic phenomenon at the gel point.  Measurements are performed on vinyl-terminated di-Me siloxane model networks with balanced stoichiometry for which the crosslinking reaction is stopped at different degrees of conversion.  At the gel point, the loss and storage moduli are congruent and proportional to ω1/2 over a wide range of temp. (-50 to +180°) and 5 decases of frequency ω.  The hypothesis is made that this behavior is valid in the entire range 0 &lt; ω &lt; ∞.  This congruence hypothesis is consistent with the Kramers-Kronig relation and leads to a constitutive equation which shows that congruent functions G'(ω) = G''(ω) (G' = storage modulus, G'' = loss modulus) are as much a rheol. property at the gel point as are infinite viscosity and zero equil. modulus.  This makes it now possible to measure exactly the instant of gelation of a crosslinking polymer without having to stop the crosslinking reaction.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqjBseBOfpNfbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh-LYUyPW_Rjg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaL28Xks1Wgsbs%253D&amp;md5=e06030c60b008c8c9dde1165ce2bd68d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1021/ja01619a008"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Williams, M.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The temperature dependence of relaxation mechanisms in amorphous polymers and other glass-forming liquids</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Williams, Malcolm L.; Landel, Robert F.; Ferry, John D.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">An empirical function, aT, is used to describe the temp. dependence of all mech. and elec. relaxation processes for amorphous polymers above their glass transition temps., Tg.  If a suitable reference temp., Ts, is chosen for each system and if log aT is plotted against T - Ts, curves are shown to coincide for the polymers, organic glass-forming liquids, and inorganic glasses investigated.  For polyisobutylene and polystyrene polymers of varying mol. wt., Ts - Tg is const.  Data in the literature were used to calc. aT from the relation, aT = ηTsρs/ηsT, where η is viscosity and ρ is d.  The org. liquids studied were glucose, abietic acid, dimethylthianthrene, PrOH, propylene glycol, and glycerol.  B2O3 and 3 optical glasses were compared.  For a series of polymers, Ts - Tg = 50 ± 5°.  Empirically, the relation, log aT = -17.44(T - Tg)/(51.6 + T - Tg), holds.  The expression of the temp. dependence of relaxation mechanisms in terms of an apparent activation energy has limited usefulness.  A theoretical relation derived for aT is: log aT = -(1/2.303fg)(T - Tg)/(fg/α2 + T - Tg), where fg is the fractional free vol at Tg and α2 is the difference between the thermal expansion coeffs. above and below Tg.  The equation is identical in form to the empirical relation.  Values of α2 and fg were 4.8 × 10-4/degree and 0.025, resp.  The value of α2 agrees with measured values for several amorphous polymers, and the value of fg appears to be reasonable.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqJmq_dRK1DdrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh-LYUyPW_Rjg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaG2MXnt1CltQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=27dd24647e57faeea98547f6b0e4503f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1016/j.ssi.2003.09.007"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nicotera, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Coppola, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oliviero, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Russo, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ranieri, G.                 10.1016/j.ssi.2003.09.007</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D167%26publication_year%3D2004%26pages%3D213-220%26journal%3DSolid%2BState%2BIonics%26author%3DI.%2BNicotera%26author%3DL.%2BCoppola%26author%3DC.%2BOliviero%26author%3DA.%2BRusso%26author%3DG.%2BA.%2BRanieri%26title%3DSome%2BPhysicochemical%2BProperties%2Bof%2BPAN-Based%2BElectrolytes%253A%2BSolution%2Band%2BGel%2BMicrostructures%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.ssi.2003.09.007&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.0c22464&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.ssi.2003.09.007&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Some physicochemical properties of PAN-based electrolytes: solution and gel microstructures</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nicotera, Isabella; Coppola, Luigi; Oliviero, Cesare; Russo, Alessandro; Ranieri, Giuseppe Antonio</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Solid State Ionics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2004</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">167</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3-4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">213-220</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SSIOD3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0167-2738</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Science B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The mech. and electrochem. properties of gel electrolytes, formed by immobilizing ethylene carbonate (EC)-propylene carbonate (PC)/lithium perchlorate (LiClO4) solns. in a polyacrylonitrile (PAN) matrix, were studied by oscillating rheol. expts., cond. measurements and 1H-NMR spectroscopy.  The gel's rheol. behavior showed two thermo-reversible structural transitions in the temp. range 25-120 °C independent from the salt content in the membranes but can be attributed to the only polymeric matrix.  The authors also report a study of the EC-PC/LiClO4 solns. in a wide concn. range performed by pulsed gradient spin-echo NMR (PGSE-NMR) technique.  The solvent self-diffusion coeff. measurements have allowed elaborating a model to describe the solvation mechanism of the lithium ions in these solns.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrpDiIZZuHy3rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh-LYUyPW_Rjg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2cXjtF2qtr8%253D&amp;md5=ab3268fccc8313efa11e9a744b45aa6a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1002/masy.200750132"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nicotera, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Coppola, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oliviero, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ranieri, G. A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Spectromechanical Properties of Polymeric Gel Electrolytes and Blends</span>. <i>Macromol. Symp.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2007</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>247</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">282</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">294</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/masy.200750132</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D247%26publication_year%3D2007%26pages%3D282-294%26journal%3DMacromol.%2BSymp.%26author%3DI.%2BNicotera%26author%3DL.%2BCoppola%26author%3DC.%2BOliviero%26author%3DG.%2BA.%2BRanieri%26title%3DSpectromechanical%2BProperties%2Bof%2BPolymeric%2BGel%2BElectrolytes%2Band%2BBlends%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fmasy.200750132&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.0c22464&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fmasy.200750132&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Spectromechanical properties of polymeric gel electrolytes and blends</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nicotera, I.; Coppola, L.; Oliviero, C.; Ranieri, G. A.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Macromolecular Symposia</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2007</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">247</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">Times of Polymers and Composites</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">282-294</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MSYMEC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1022-1360</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this paper we studied the spectro-mech. properties of polymer gel electrolytes and blends by means of shear rheol.  These electrolytes were obtained by immobilizing EC/PC/LiClO4 solns. in a polymeric matrix of PEO, PAN and PMMA, resp.  Two structural and thermo-reversible transitions, a strong-to-weak gel and a gel-to-sol, were revealed and discussed.  Moreover, PMMA-PVdF blends have been studied as a function of the different polymeric ratios in order to obtain the best compromise between ionic conduction and mech. properties.  Interesting mech. properties were obsd. at some intermediate blend compns.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGquFqFaAZOKMLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhcWWP8dGMkSA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2sXjslWqu7Y%253D&amp;md5=e189c21021f532d8796028fcc1d95fc9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1039/C9EE00283A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cho, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, Y.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Critical Design Factors for Kinetically Favorable P-Based Compounds toward Alloying with Na Ions for High-Power Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Environ. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1326</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1333</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C9EE00283A</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D12%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D1326-1333%26journal%3DEnergy%2BEnviron.%2BSci.%26author%3DD.%2BKim%26author%3DK.%2BZhang%26author%3DM.%2BCho%26author%3DY.-M.%2BKang%26title%3DCritical%2BDesign%2BFactors%2Bfor%2BKinetically%2BFavorable%2BP-Based%2BCompounds%2Btoward%2BAlloying%2Bwith%2BNa%2BIons%2Bfor%2BHigh-Power%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC9EE00283A&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.0c22464&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC9EE00283A&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Critical design factors for kinetically favorable P-based compounds toward alloying with Na ions for high-power sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Duho; Zhang, Kai; Cho, Maenghyo; Kang, Yong-Mook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1326-1333</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">First-principles calcns. with exptl. validation enable us to radically predict and compare the electron transport, elastic softness, and thermodn. phase stabilities of black phosphorus (BP) and GeP3 to figure out the crucial factors for designing the most kinetically favorable P-based compds. toward alloying with Na ions.  From the viewpoint of electron transport, Ge is able to provide P with electrons due to the difference of electronegativity, causing GeP3 to have a significantly reduced band gap and a lower electron-hopping barrier compared to BP.  Because the structure of GeP3 looks more elastically softened than that of BP, its Na+ migration barriers in the sodiated states must be lower than those of the sodiated BP structure as proven by the higher Na+ diffusion coeffs. of GeP3.  The thermodn. phase stabilities of BP and GeP3 could be predicted by calcg. their mixing enthalpy values and thereby homogeneous bulk free energies were obtained for Na1-x(GeP3) (0.0 ≤ x ≤ 0.5) indicating that no phase sepn. occurs in the sodiated GeP3 because of an addnl. stable single-phase at x = 0.25.  By contrast, the sodiated P easily gets sepd. into NaP and Na0.5P with the same sodiation content.  The suppressed phase sepn. in GeP3 makes the Na+ distribution homogeneous as confirmed by TEM-EDS color mapping and thus contributes to increasing Na+ diffusion coeffs. because Na+ migration can be primarily interrupted by the interfaces or grain boundaries between the sepd. phases.  Taking into account three enhanced physicochem. properties, the GeP3 electrodes may well present a superior rate capability to the BP electrode, underscoring that electron transport, elastic softness, and thermodn. phase stabilities must be the most important design factors for realizing kinetically favorable P-based compds. toward alloying with Na+.  In detail, even at an ultrahigh c.d. of 20 A g-1, the capacity of the GeP3 electrode still comes to 0.197 A h g-1.  At 1 A g-1, GeP3 could maintain a discharge capacity of 0.499 A h g-1 even after 1000 cycles.  This study may provide promising guidelines for the design of alloy-based electrode materials for high power and energy SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpuohmt-cRMxrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhcWWP8dGMkSA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXjt1ertrk%253D&amp;md5=e99bce6c29c7ff032153d09282e7b068</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da87218abfb325-SJC">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30'],'ref31':['cit31'],'ref32':['cit32'],'ref33':['cit33'],'ref34':['cit34'],'ref35':['cit35'],'ref36':['cit36'],'ref37':['cit37'],'ref38':['cit38'],'ref39':['cit39'],'ref40':['cit40'],'ref41':['cit41'],'ref42':['cit42'],'ref43':['cit43'],'ref44':['cit44'],'ref45':['cit45'],'ref46':['cit46']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy d. is the main property of rechargeable batteries that has driven the entire technol. forward in past decades.  Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) now surpass other, previously competitive battery types (for example, lead-acid and nickel metal hydride) but still require extensive further improvement to, in particular, extend the operation hours of mobile IT devices and the driving mileages of all-elec. vehicles.  In this Review, we present a crit. overview of a wide range of post-LIB materials and systems that could have a pivotal role in meeting such demands.  We divide battery systems into two categories: near-term and long-term technologies.  To provide a realistic and balanced perspective, we describe the operating principles and remaining issues of each post-LIB technol., and also evaluate these materials under com. cell configurations.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpmrufRRuizrLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljKOaRWeQ6icw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhtVert7k%253D&amp;md5=3d2782c5ebf801e43442f01f2206379f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2016.07.023"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Casimir, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ogoke, O.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Amine, J.                         rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Silicon-based anodes for lithium-ion batteries: Effectiveness of materials synthesis and electrode preparation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Casimir, Anix; Zhang, Hanguang; Ogoke, Ogechi; Amine, Joseph C.; Lu, Jun; Wu, Gang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithium-ion batteries are widely used throughout the world for portable electronic devices and mobile phones and show great potential for more demanding applications like elec. vehicles.  Unfortunately, lithium-ion batteries still lack the required level of energy storage to completely meet the demands of such applications as elec. vehicles.  Among advanced materials being studied, silicon nanoparticles have demonstrated great potential as an anode material to replace the commonly used graphite.  Silicon has been shown to have a high theor. gravimetric capacity, approx. 4200 mA h/g, compared to only 372 mA h/g for graphite.  Though silicon nanoparticles have remarkably high capacity, they suffer from rapid degrdn. with each cycle due to electrode vol. expansion of approx. 400% during lithiation, placing a large strain on the material.  With each cycle that strain creates cracks in the electrode particles and causes them to break down into smaller particles, which create void spaces between the particles and lead to poor contact as reflected in poor cond.  In this review, we discuss exciting new research on silicon-based anodes conducted during the past couple of years.  Besides stressing the importance of well-designed nanostructures of Si, we focus on optimization of the Si electrode and resulting performance enhancement by properly selecting binders and synergistically integrating them with various carbon materials during electrode design and fabrication.  Importantly, although each improvement strategy has its own advantage, appropriate combination of them will yield much higher anode performance.  We summarize the core issues in developing the silicon anode and effective strategies in yielding more promising results.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGranonB1DzdKbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh98wk2yHPjWA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xht12nsrjK&amp;md5=80307ce2bdcff0e95e389526f6e535ca</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201702849"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Advanced Phosphorus-Based Materials for Lithium/Sodium-Ion Batteries: Recent Developments and Future Perspectives</span>. <i>Adv.
